PigeonBlog Recuperation and staying with the trouble are the themes of [my]0-i sf practice . It is all too possible to address these questions through human brutality toward pigeons , or indeed through pigeon damage to other species or to human - built structures . Instead , [I]0-i want to turn to the differential burdens of urban air pollution that contribute to different rates of human ( and other - than - human , but that is not rated ) mortality and illness , often distributed by race and [class]720-class . [Working pigeons]721-working pigeons will be [[our]722-our companions]723-our companions in projects of environmental justice in [California]28-california that seek to repair [both blighted neighborhoods]724-both blighted neighborhoods and social relations . [We]722-our will stay with the trouble in the tissues of an art activism project called [PigeonBlog]310-pigeonblog . This was a project by [artist - researcher [Beatriz da Costa]304-beatriz da costa]725-artist - researcher beatriz da costa with [[her]725-artist - researcher beatriz da costa students]726-her students [Cina Hazegh]305-cina hazegh and [Kevin Ponto]306-kevin ponto ; [they]727-they tied sf patterns with many human , animal , and cyborg coshapers . In August 2006 , racing pigeons flew as participants in three public social experiments that intimately joined communication technologies with [city people]728-city people and urban sporting birds . The pigeons flew once as part of a Seminar in Experimental Critical Theory at [the University of [California]28-california at [Irvine]31-irvine]30-the university of california at irvine and twice for the festival called Seven Days of Art and Interconnectivity of [the Inter - Society for Electronic Arts in [San Jose]33-san jose]32-the inter - society for electronic arts in san jose , California.23 PigeonBlog required extensive collaboration between “ homing pigeons , [artists]2674-artists , [engineers]2675-engineers , and [pigeon fanciers]2676-pigeon fanciers engaged in a grass - roots scientific data gathering initiative designed to collect and distribute information about air quality conditions to [the general public]2677-the general public . ”24[729-working - class people in relations of competitive masculine sport and profound cross - species affection] Worldwide , racing pigeons are no strangers to alliances with [working - class people in relations of competitive masculine sport and profound cross - species affection]729-working - class people in relations of competitive masculine sport and profound cross - species affection , and [their]730-their historical capabilities in surveillance and communication technologies and networks are very old and very important . These pigeons have been [workers]731-workers and [subjects in ornithology and psychology research labs]732-subjects in ornithology and psychology research labs for many decades . But sporting homing pigeons had not , before PigeonBlog , been invited to join all of that heritage together with [another set of players]733-another set of players , namely , [art activists]734-art activists . The project sought to join savvy , inexpensive , do - it - yourself electronics with citizen science and interspecies coproduced art and knowledge “ in the pursuit of resistant action . ”25[307-da costa] The data were intended to provoke , motivate , amplify , inspire , and illustrate , not to substitute for or surpass professional air pollution science and monitoring . [Da Costa]307-da costa set out not to become [an air pollution scientist]735-an air pollution scientist , but to spark collaboration in something quite different : multispecies art in action for mundane worlds in need of — and capable of — recuperation across consequential differences . [These sites]739-these sites often cluster in and near [the neighborhoods of [working - class people]741-working - class people , [people of color]742-people of color , and [immigrants]743-immigrants]740-the neighborhoods of working - class people , people of color , and immigrants — hardly mutually exclusive categories . Official government air pollution monitoring devices in [Southern California]1-southern california are placed at fixed points away from [high - traffic areas]744-high - traffic areas and [known pollution sources]745-known pollution sources and at altitudes higher than [the zones in which [people]622-people and lots of other plants and animals breathe]746-the zones in which people and lots of other plants and animals breathe . Each monitoring device costs many thousands of dollars and can only measure gases in [its]748-its immediate vicinity , relying on various models to extrapolate to the volume of the air basin . [Properly equipped racing pigeons]749-properly equipped racing pigeons can gather continuous real - time air pollution data while moving through the air at key heights not accessible to the official instruments , as well as from the ground where they are released for [their]749-properly equipped racing pigeons homing flights . What happens when human exceptionalism and bounded individualism , those old saws of Western philosophy and political economics , become unthinkable in the best sciences , whether natural or social ? [The earth of [the ongoing Chthulucene]977-the ongoing chthulucene]976-the earth of the ongoing chthulucene is sympoietic , not autopoietic . After [I]0-i used the term sympoiesis in a grasp for something other than the lures of autopoiesis , [Katie King]327-katie king told [me]0-i about [M. Beth Dempster]328-m. beth dempster ’s Master of Environmental Studies thesis written in 1998 , in which [she]328-m. beth dempster suggested the term sympoiesis for “ collectively - producing systems that do not have self - defined spatial or temporal boundaries . Information and control are distributed among components . The systems are evolutionary and have the potential for surprising change . ”[328-m. beth dempster] By contrast , autopoietic systems are “ self - producing ”[328-m. beth dempster] autonomous units “ with self defined spatial or temporal boundaries that tend to be centrally controlled , homeostatic , and predictable . ”13[328-m. beth dempster] [Dempster]328-m. beth dempster argued that many systems are mistaken for autopoietic that are really sympoietic . Tentacular Thinking

Symbiogenesis and the Lively Arts of Staying with the Trouble

Symbiogenesis

Sympoiesis is a simple word ; it means “ making - with . ”[1296-they] Nothing makes itself ; nothing is really autopoietic or self - organizing . In the words of the Inupiat computer “ world game , ”[1296-they] [earthlings]1298-earthlings are never alone.1 That is the radical implication of sympoiesis . Sympoiesis is a word proper to complex , dynamic , responsive , situated , historical systems . It is a word for worlding - with , in company . Sympoiesis enfolds autopoiesis and generatively unfurls and extends it . The vivid four - by - six - foot painting called Endosymbiosis hangs in [the hallway]1299-the hallway joining [the Departments of Geosciences and Biology at UMass [Amherst]120-amherst]119-the departments of geosciences and biology at umass amherst , near [the Life and Earth Café]1300-the life and earth café , surely a spatial clue to how critters become - with each other.2 Perhaps as sensual molecular curiosity and definitely as insatiable hunger , irresistible attraction toward enfolding each other is the vital motor of living and dying on [earth]511-earth . [Critters]392-critters interpenetrate [one another]697-one another , loop around and through [one another]697-one another , eat each another , get indigestion , and partially digest and partially assimilate [one another]697-one another , and thereby establish sympoietic arrangements that are otherwise known as cells , organisms , and ecological assemblages .

Endosymbiosis : Homage to [Lynn Margulis]353-margulis , [Shoshanah Dubiner]393-shoshanah dubiner , 2012 . www.cybermuse.com .

Another word for these sympoietic entities is holobionts , or , etymologically , “ [entire beings ”[393-shoshanah dubiner] or “ safe and sound beings]2724-entire beings ” or “ safe and sound beings . ”3[393-shoshanah dubiner] That is decidedly not the same thing as [One and Individual]1305-one and individual . Rather , in polytemporal , polyspatial knottings , holobionts hold together contingently and dynamically , engaging [other holobionts]1306-other holobionts in complex patternings . [Critters]392-critters do not precede [their]392-critters relatings ; [they]392-critters make each other through semiotic material involution , out of the beings of previous such entanglements . [Lynn Margulis]353-margulis knew a great deal about “ the intimacy of [strangers]2725-strangers , ”[353-margulis] a phrase [she]353-margulis proposed to describe the most fundamental practices of critters becoming - with each other at every node of intraaction in earth history . [I]0-i propose holoents as a general term to replace “ [units ”[353-margulis] or “ beings]2726-units ” or “ beings . ”[353-margulis] Like [Margulis]353-margulis , [I]0-i use holobiont to mean symbiotic assemblages , at whatever scale of space or time , which are more like knots of diverse intra - active relatings in dynamic complex systems , than like the entities of a biology made up of preexisting bounded units ( genes , cells , organisms , etc . ) in interactions that can only be conceived as competitive or cooperative . Like [hers]353-margulis , [my]0-i use of holobiont does not designate host + symbionts because [all of [the players]518-the players]1307-all of the players are symbionts to [each other]635-each other , in diverse kinds of relationalities and with varying degrees of openness to attachments and assemblages with other holobionts . Symbiosis is not a synonym for “ mutually beneficial . ”[353-margulis] The array of names needed to designate the heterogeneous webbed patterns and processes of situated and dynamic dilemmas and advantages for the symbionts / holobionts is only beginning to surface as [biologists]1310-biologists let go of the dictates of possessive individualism and zero - sum games as the template for explanation . [An adept in the study of microbes , cell biology , chemistry , geology , and paleogeography]1311-an adept in the study of microbes , cell biology , chemistry , geology , and paleogeography , as well as [a lover of languages , arts]1312-a lover of languages , arts , stories , systems theories , and alarmingly generative critters , including [human beings]605-human beings , [Margulis]353-margulis was [a radical evolutionary theorist]1314-a radical evolutionary theorist . [Her]353-margulis first and most intense loves were the bacteria and archaea of [Terra]65-terra and all [their]1315-their bumptious doings . The core of [Margulis]353-margulis ’s view of life was that new kinds of cells , tissues , organs , and species evolve primarily through the long - lasting intimacy of [strangers]2725-strangers . The fusion of genomes in symbioses , followed by natural selection — with a very modest role for mutation as a motor of system level change — leads to increasingly complex levels of goodenough quasi - individuality to get through the day , or the aeon . [Margulis]353-margulis called this basic and mortal life - making process symbiogenesis . [Bacteria]394-bacteria and archaea did it first . [My]0-i sense is that in [her]353-margulis heart of hearts [Margulis]353-margulis felt that bacteria and archaea did it all , and there was n’t much left for [so - called higher - order biological entities]1317-so - called higher - order biological entities to do or invent . Eventually , however , by fusing with each other in stabilized , ongoing ways , archaea and bacteria invented the modern complex cell , with its nucleus full of ropy chromosomes made of dna and proteins , and diverse other sorts of extranuclear organelles , from undulating whips and spinning blades for locomotion to specialized vesicles and tubules for a zillion functions that work better kept a bit separate from each other.4 Because [she]353-margulis was a founder of Gaia theory with [James Lovelock]352-james lovelock and [a student of interlocked and multileveled systemic processes of nonreductionist organization and maintenance that make [earth]511-earth [itself]511-earth and earth ’s living beings]1318-a student of interlocked and multileveled systemic processes of nonreductionist organization and maintenance that make earth itself and earth ’s living beings unique , [Margulis]353-margulis called these processes autopoietic.5 Perhaps [she]353-margulis would have chosen the term sympoietic , but the word and concept had not yet surfaced.6 As long as autopoiesis does not mean self - sufficient “ self making , ”[353-margulis] autopoiesis and sympoiesis , foregrounding and backgrounding different aspects of systemic complexity , are in generative friction , or generative enfolding , rather than opposition . In 1998 , [a Canadian environmental studies graduate student]1320-a canadian environmental studies graduate student named [M. Beth Dempster]328-m. beth dempster suggested the term sympoiesis for “ collectivelyproducing systems that do not have self - defined spatial or temporal boundaries . Information and control are distributed among components . The systems are evolutionary and have the potential for surprising change . ”[1320-a canadian environmental studies graduate student] By contrast , [autopoietic systems]1321-autopoietic systems are “ self - producing ”[1320-a canadian environmental studies graduate student] autonomous units “ with self defined spatial or temporal boundaries that tend to be centrally controlled , homeostatic , and predictable . ”7[1320-a canadian environmental studies graduate student] Symbiosis makes trouble for autopoiesis , and symbiogenesis is an even bigger troublemaker for self - organizing individual units . Since [Darwin]292-darwin ’s On the Origin of Species in 1859 , biological evolutionary theory has become more and more essential to [our]1326-we ability to think , feel , and act well ; and the interlinked Darwinian sciences that came together roughly between the 1930s and 1950s into “ the Modern Synthesis ”[396-theodosius dobzhansky] or “ New Synthesis ”[396-theodosius dobzhansky] remain astonishing . How could [one]544-one be [a serious person]1332-a serious person and not honor such works as [Theodosius Dobzhansky]396-theodosius dobzhansky ’s Genetics and the Origin of Species ( 1937 ) , [Ernst Mayr]397-ernst mayr ’s Systematics and the Origin of Species ( 1942 ) , [George Gaylord Simpson]398-george gaylord simpson ’s Tempo and Mode in Evolution ( 1944 ) , and even [Richard Dawkins]399-richard dawkins ’s later sociobiological formulations within the Modern Synthesis , The Selfish Gene ( 1976 ) ? However , bounded units ( code fragments , genes , cells , organisms , populations , species , ecosystems ) and relations described mathematically in competition equations are virtually the only actors and story formats of the Modern Synthesis . Evolutionary momentum , always verging on modernist notions of progress , is a constant theme , although teleology in the strict sense is not . Even as these sciences lay the groundwork for scientific conceptualization of the Anthropocene , they are undone in the very thinking of Anthropocene systems that require enfolded autopoietic and sympoietic analysis . Rooted in units and relations , especially competitive relations , the sciences of the Modern Synthesis , for example , population genetics , have a hard time with four key biological domains : embryology and de62 c h a p t e r t h r e e

velopment , symbiosis and collaborative entanglements of holobionts and holobiomes , the vast worldings of microbes , and exuberant critter biobehavioral inter- and intra - actions.10 Approaches tuned to “ multispecies becoming - with ”[1326-we] better sustain [us]1326-we in staying with the trouble on terra . An emerging “ New New Synthesis”—an[1326-we] extended synthesis — in transdisciplinary biologies and arts proposes string figures tying together human and nonhuman ecologies , evolution , development , history , affects , performances , technologies , and more . Indebted first to [Margulis]353-margulis , [I]0-i can only sketch a few aspects of the “ Extended Evolutionary Synthesis ”[353-margulis] unfolding in the early twenty - first century.11 Forming part of [her]353-margulis cosmopolitan heritage , formulations of symbiogenesis predate [Margulis]353-margulis in the early twentieth - century work of [the Russian Konstantin Mereschkowsky]400-the russian konstantin mereschkowsky and others.12 However , [Margulis]353-margulis , [[her]353-margulis successors]1333-her successors , and [[her]353-margulis colleagues]1334-her colleagues bring together symbiogenetic imaginations and materialities with all of the powerful cyborg tools of the late twentieth - century molecular and ultrastructural biological revolutions , including electron microscopes , nucleic acid sequencers , immunoassay techniques , immense and comparative genomic and proteomic databases , and more . The strength of the Extended Synthesis is precisely in the intellectual , cultural , and technical convergence that makes it possible to develop new model systems , concrete experimental practices , research collaborations , and both verbal and mathematical explanatory instruments . Such a convergence was materially impossible before the s and after . A model is a work object ; a model is not the same kind of thing as a metaphor or analogy . A model is worked , and it does work . Although multicellular plants appeared on [earth]511-earth half a million years earlier , because of its robustness and sympoietic richness , [I]0-i focus on a proposed model system for the emergence of animal multicellularity . Every living thing has emerged and persevered ( or not ) bathed and swaddled in bacteria and archaea . Truly nothing is sterile ; and that reality is a terrific danger , basic fact of life , and critter - making opportunity . Using molecular and comparative genomic approaches and proposing infectious — symbiogenetic — processes , [[Nicole King]403-king ’s laboratory]1354-nicole king ’s laboratory at [the University of [California]28-california , [Berkeley]123-berkeley]122-the university of california , berkeley , works to reconstruct possible origins and development of animal multicellularity.14 [These scientists]1355-these scientists show that interspecies — really , interkingdom — meetings and enfoldings can produce entities that hold together , develop , communicate , and form layered tissues like animals do . As [Alegado]404-alegado and [King]403-king put it , Comparisons among modern animals and [their]1356-their closest living relatives , the choanoflagellates , suggest that the first animals used flagellated collar cells to capture bacterial prey . The cell biology of prey capture , such as cell adhesion between predator and prey , involves mechanisms that may have been co - opted to mediate intercellular interactions during the evolution of animal multicellularity . Moreover , a history of bacterivory may have influenced the evolution of animal genomes by driving the evolution of genetic pathways for immunity and facilitating lateral gene transfer . Understanding the interactions between bacteria and the progenitors of animals may help to explain the myriad ways in which bacteria shape the biology of modern animals , including ourselves.15 In Marilyn Strathern ’s sense , partial connections abound . Getting hungry , eating , and partially digesting , partially assimilating , and partially transforming : these are the actions of [companion species]515-companion species . [King]403-king ’s ambitious program is crafting a stabilized and genomically well - characterized model system of cultures of choanoflagellates ( Salpingoeca rosetta ) and bacteria from the genus Algoriphagus to investigate critical aspects of the formation of multicellular animals . Choanoflagellates can live as either single cells or multicellular colonies ; what determines the transitions ? The close evolutionary relationship between choanoflagellates and animals lends strength to the model.16 The symbiogenetic theory of origins of multicellularity is contested ; there are attractive alternate explanations . What distinguishes [[King]403-king ’s lab]1358-king ’s lab is its production of a model system that is experimentally tractable , transferable in principle to other sites , and generative of testable questions at the heart of being animal . To be animal is to become - with bacteria ( and , no doubt , viruses and many other sorts of critters ; a basic aspect of sympoiesis is its expandable set of [players]983-players ) . No wonder [the best science writers]1360-the best science writers bring [[Nicole King]403-king ’s lab]1361-nicole king ’s lab into [my]0-i dinner conversations on a regular basis.17 Next , [I]0-i hold out a tasty model system for studying developmental Sympoiesis

symbioses . The question here is not how animals hold [themselves]1362-they together at all , but rather , how [they]1362-they craft developmental patternings that take [them]1362-they through time in astonishing morphogeneses . [My]0-i favorite model is the diminutive Hawaiian bobtail squid , Euprymna scolopes , and its bacterial symbionts , Vibrio fischeri , which are essential for the squid ’s constructing [its]1363-its ventral pouch that houses luminescing bacteria , so that the hunting squid can look like a starry sky to its prey below on dark nights , or appear not to cast a shadow on moonlit nights . Beaded jellyfish made by [Vonda N. McIntyre]164-vonda n. mcintyre for the [Crochet Coral Reef]202-the crochet coral reef . From the collection of [the Institute for Figuring ( IFF]1625-the institute for figuring ( iff ) . Photograph © IFF .

from [Ireland]166-ireland , [Latvia]167-latvia , [the United Arab Emirates]1626-the united arab emirates , [Australia]49-australia , [the United States]1076-the united states , [the UK]1628-the uk , [Croatia]168-croatia , and more — have come together to crochet in wool , cotton , plastic bags , discarded reel - to - reel tape , vinyl jelly yarn , Saran wrap , and just about anything else that can be induced to loop and whirl in the codes of crocheting . The code is so simple : crocheted models of hyperbolic planes achieve their ruffled forms by progressively increasing the number of stitches in each row . The emergent vitalities of this wooly experimental life - form take diverse corporeal shape as [crafters]1629-crafters increase the numbers from row to row irregularly , oddly , whimsically , or strictly to see what forms [they]1629-crafters could make — not just any forms , but crenulated beings that take life as marine critters of [the vulnerable reefs.45 “ Every woolen form]2738-the vulnerable reefs.45 “ every woolen form has [its]2738-the vulnerable reefs.45 “ every woolen form fibrous dna . ”46[2738-the vulnerable reefs.45 “ every woolen form] But wool is hardly the only material . Never Alone ( [Kisima Ingitchuna]442-kisima ingitchuna ) [My]0-i third example of science art worlding for living on [a damaged planet]1377-a damaged planet is making “ world games . ”[442-kisima ingitchuna] World games are made with and from [indigenous peoples]1174-indigenous peoples ’ stories and practices . “ But what good are old stories if the wisdom they contain is not shared?”64[442-kisima ingitchuna] These games both remember and create worlds in dangerous times ; they are worlding practices . [Indigenous peoples around [the earth]941-the earth]1803-indigenous peoples around the earth have a particular angle on the discourses of coming extinctions and exterminations of the Anthropocene and Capitalocene.65 The idea that disaster will come is not new ; disaster , indeed genocide and devastated [home places]1805-home places , has already come , decades and centuries ago , and it has not stopped . The resurgence of [peoples]640-peoples and of places is nurtured with ragged vitality in the teeth of such loss , mourning , memory , resilience , reinvention of what it means to be native , refusal to deny irreversible destruction , and refusal to disengage from living and dying well in presents and futures . World games require inventive , sympoietic collaborations that bring together such things as [computer game platforms]1807-computer game platforms and [[their]1807-computer game platforms designers]1808-their designers , [indigenous storytellers]1809-indigenous storytellers , [visual artists]1810-visual artists , [carvers and puppet makers]1811-carvers and puppet makers , [digital - savvy youngsters]1812-digital - savvy youngsters , and [community activists]1813-community activists . A refrain from Navajo prayers often accompanies [a weaver]1879-a weaver ’s work : “ With [me]1879-a weaver there is beauty ”[1879-a weaver] ( shil hózhó ) ; “ in [me]1879-a weaver there is beauty ”[1879-a weaver] ( shii ’ hózhó ) ; “ from [me]1879-a weaver beauty radiates ”[1879-a weaver] ( shits ’ áá d óó hózhó).76 Hózhó is a central concept in Navajo cosmology and daily practice . Usual translations into English are “ beauty , ”[1879-a weaver] “ harmony , ”[1879-a weaver] and “ order ”[1879-a weaver] ; but [I]0-i think a better translation would emphasize right relations of [the world]541-the world , including human and [nonhuman beings]1881-nonhuman beings , who are of [the world]541-the world as its storied and dynamic substance , not in [the world]541-the world as a container . For [the Diné]419-diné , greed is the greatest source of disorder ; it destroys right relations at [their]419-diné root . Weaving is a useful practice , to be sure , and an economic one ; but , fundamentally , weaving is also cosmological performance , knotting proper relationality and connectedness into the warp and weft of the fabric.77 The geometric patterns of repetition and invention in weaving are performances of Diné stories and knowledge ; the patterns propose and embody world - making and world - sustaining relations . The dynamic patterning continues in contemporary weavings , many of which explore new as well as inherited themes , colors , stories , and fibers.78 Weavings are individual ; they are made by [a particular woman]1886-a particular woman and embody [her]1886-a particular woman style and sensibility , recognizable by knowledgeable members of the community.79 Names of [weavers]1887-weavers and [weavers]1887-weavers ’ lineages matter , but weavings are not made to be possessed as property . Neither that nor the entanglement of the creative personal and the cosmological is a contradiction . Weaving is neither secular nor religious ; it is sensible . It performs and manifests the meaningful lived connections for sustaining kinship , behavior , relational action — for hózhó — for [humans]594-humans and [nonhumans]595-nonhumans . Situated worlding is ongoing , neither traditional nor modern . The art of weaving and care of Churro sheep reciprocally enact Diné relations of natural and cosmic order . [The boundaries of [the reservation]1912-the reservation]1911-the boundaries of the reservation extended gradually until the 1930s ; and , despite the failure of [the U.S. government]1913-the u.s. government after the Diné return from [Bosque Redondo]205-bosque redondo to provide promised stock , sheep flocks grew much faster than [the human population]1914-the human population . This growth was partly driven by the trading post system , which turned wool into blankets to realize value and bought these blankets by the pound in a system of perpetual indebtedness . To obtain basic necessities in this system of debt , [the Navajo]422-navajo were forced to produce more and more wool from more and more sheep . [The traders]1915-the traders sold the weavings in the art and tourist market , but purchased [the women]1916-the women ’s weavings as if they were low - value raw wool . Despite the efforts of [federal agents]1917-federal agents , [most of [the Diné]419-diné]1918-most of the diné continued to prefer multipurpose , hardy Churro sheep to merinos and other “ improved ”[419-diné] breeds . [Sheep]422-navajo , goats , horses , and cattle were all part of the pattern of Navajo pastoralism , ordered by complex [clan and gender relationships]1919-clan and gender relationships . [The animals]1920-the animals and [the people]592-the people made kin together.82 Sheep and goats were especially crucial for [women]1634-women ’s abilities to feed and provision [[their]1634-women families]1923-their families , as well as to [their]1634-women authority in the clans . With intensifying erosion , severe grazing , and sustained drought , by the 1930s the system was increasingly out of harmony , a condition recognized by both whites and [Navajos]455-navajos . The second intense efforts of [the U.S. government]1913-the u.s. government to exterminate [Navajo]422-navajo - Churro sheep occurred in this context ; like the first originary trauma , this lethal event can be neither forgotten nor effectively mourned . It bears evil fruit to this day . Restoring [the land]898-the land , animals , and [people]622-people to hózhó is an ongoing process that continues to require continuous weaving . The colonial and capitalist structures of both exterminations have not been dismantled . The first Churro sheep extermination was conducted by [U.S. military men]1927-u.s. military men ; the second was also conducted by force , this time by [U.S. progressive agricultural authorities within the ideology and apparatus of the New Deal]1928-u.s. progressive agricultural authorities within the ideology and apparatus of the new deal . [These officials]1929-these officials worked within the ecological concept of carrying capacity , the patriarchal colonial concepts of [male - headed households]1930-male - headed households , and [the modernizers]1931-the modernizers ’ concepts of progress . Without asking how colonial economic structures like the unequal wool trade might be a significant cause of both poverty and ecological damage and judging the erosion of [Navajo lands]1932-navajo lands to be due to overstocking as a biological sort of fact , U.S. government scientists in [the Department of Agriculture]1933-the department of agriculture and others in killed most of [the women]1916-the women ’s goats , the primary source of subsistence meat for [families]1935-families . White - settler divisions of [the world]541-the world into nature and culture split Navajo lifeways into colonial apparatuses of ecology and economics , practiced by different sorts of [scientific specialists who could not systematically think even with each other]1937-scientific specialists who could not systematically think even with each other , much less with [Navajo herders]1893-navajo herders and [weavers]1887-weavers . In 1935 , [officials]1900-officials killed vast numbers of sheep . Churro sheep , many known individually by [[their]1941-their people]603-their people , were preferentially killed , often in front of [[their]1941-their human families]1943-their human families . Evident in photographs , piles of bones from these animal murders were still prominent in the 1970s ; and [people]622-people still dramatically narrated the trauma , even describing particular animals in [their]622-people flocks . Following the killing of about a million sheep and goats ( without significant compensation to this day ) , stocking quotas were imposed , and collective ownership of [land]1529-land was not recognized . The census by which stock quotas and permits were allocated recognized [only heads of [households]1947-households , who could not be [married women]1948-married women]1946-only heads of households , who could not be married women , which was a major blow to [Diné]419-diné matrifocal ways of ordering [their]622-people relations with land , animals , and each other . Transhumance was disrupted as land boundaries were redrawn into [Land Management Units]212-land management units , exacerbating erosion as both seasonal and dynamic rain - pattern - sensitive movements for grazing became difficult across such boundaries . Besides an act of scientific colonial arrogance and culpable ignorance , the animal exterminations of the s effected a profound decapitalization of [the whole people , whose existing poverty , itself linked to the consequences of the first Hwéeldi]1949-the whole people , whose existing poverty , itself linked to the consequences of the first hwéeldi , Sympoiesis

was structurally intensified . With the failure to restore the health of lands , waters , animals , and [people in hózhó]1950-people in hózhó , balanced pastoralism was not reconstructed ; resurgence on [the Colorado Plateau]1951-the colorado plateau was wounded . Stock levels and erosion remain a major problem , intensified by deep resentment of forced controls , including colonial conceptual apparatuses within [the Navajo Nation]1526-the navajo nation . In a crisis of drought and multispecies lifeways out of balance in the s , the opportunity was missed to bring scientific ecological ideas like carrying capacity into difficult but necessary conversation with Navajo concepts and practices of hózhó . Neither carrying capacity nor hózhó is a fixed , deterministic concept ; both are relational , contextual , tuned to some ways of living and dying and not others . It matters what concepts think concepts , and vice versa ; but in this case , colonial structures assured that the important concepts would not be allowed to think each other , would not be allowed perhaps to issue in something that did not yet exist in thought for [either people]1953-either people , but might be needed by both . When one system of thinking and practice can only disparage and nullify another in colonial recursions , there can be no sympoiesis and no hózhó . The consequences of the failure to invent the needed decolonial conversations ramifies into the present . There is no question that anthropogenic processes have had planetary effects , in inter / intra - action with other processes and species , for as long as [our]2040-we species can be identified ( a few tens of thousand years ) ; and agriculture has been huge ( a few thousand years ) . Of course , from the start the greatest planetary terraformers ( and [reformers ) of all]2061-reformers ) of all have been and still are bacteria and [[their]2062-their kin]1860-their kin , also in inter / intra - action of myriad kinds ( including with [people]622-people and [their]622-people practices , technological and otherwise).1 The spread of seed - dispersing plants millions of years before human agriculture was a planet - changing development , and so were many other revolutionary evolutionary ecological developmental historical events . [People]622-people joined the bumptious fray early and dynamically , even before [they]622-people / [we]2040-we were critters who were later named [Homo sapiens]942-homo sapiens . But [I]0-i think the issues about naming relevant to the Anthropocene , Plantationocene , or Capitalocene have to do with scale , rate / speed , synchronicity , and complexity . The constant questions when considering systemic phenomena have to be , When do changes in degree become changes in kind ? and What are the effects of bioculturally , biotechnically , biopolitically , historically situated people ( not [Man]359-man ) relative to , and combined with , the effects of other species assemblages and other biotic / abiotic forces ?

[Cyborgs]470-cyborgs are not [machines]2130-machines in just any sense , nor are [they]470-cyborgs [machine - organism hybrids]2131-machine - organism hybrids . In fact , [they]470-cyborgs are not hybrids at all . [They]470-cyborgs are , rather , imploded entities , dense material semiotic “ things”—articulated[470-cyborgs] string figures of ontologically heterogeneous , historically situated , materially rich , virally proliferating relatings of particular sorts , not all the time everywhere , but here , there , and in between , with consequences . Particular sorts of historically situated machines signaled by the words information and system play their part in cyborg living and dying . Particular sorts of historically situated organisms , signaled by the idioms of labor systems , energetics , and communication , play [their]470-cyborgs part . Finally , particular sorts of historically situated [human beings]605-human beings , becoming - with the practices and artifacts of technoscience , play [their]470-cyborgs part . Characterized by partial connections , the parts do not add up to any whole ; but they do add up to worlds of nonoptional , stratified , webbed , and unfinished living and dying , appearing and disappearing .
